It's not taking in the stylesheet. Should this not be it's own page with a hedaer and stylesheet link?

Yes. If your CSS isn't being applied, it's because what you've shown is only the <body> section.

Your error.html should be a complete Thymeleaf page, just like your home.html.

For example:

<!DOCTYPE html>
<html xmlns:th="http://www.thymeleaf.org">

<head>

    <title>Prompt Vault - Error</title>

    <link rel="stylesheet"
          th:href="@{/css/app.css}" />

</head>

<body>

<div class="error-page">

    <div class="error-card">

        <div class="error-icon">🌙</div>

        <h1 class="error-title">Oopsie, something went wonky</h1>

        <div class="error-code">
            Error <span th:text="${status}">500</span>
        </div>

        <p class="error-message" th:if="${status == 404}">
            This page seems to have wandered off into the prompt vault.
        </p>

        <p class="error-message" th:if="${status != 404}">
            Something unexpected happened, but don't worry — your prompts are still safe.
        </p>

        <a class="primary-btn"
           th:href="@{/home}">
            Take me home
        </a>

    </div>

</div>

</body>

</html>

A couple of other things to check:
1. File location

Make sure app.css is located at:

src/main/resources/static/css/app.css

because your Thymeleaf link:

th:href="@{/css/app.css}"

expects Spring to serve it from /css/app.css.
2. Template location

Make sure the error page is:

src/main/resources/templates/error.html

Spring Boot automatically picks this up.
3. Browser dev tools

Open Network tab and look for:

/css/app.css

If you get:

404

then the stylesheet path is wrong.

If you get:

200

then the stylesheet is loading and the issue is elsewhere.
Better option for Prompt Vault

Since users are already logged in when most errors occur, I'd actually render the error page inside your normal application layout:

<body>

<div th:replace="~{fragments/header :: header}"></div>

<div class="content">

    <div th:replace="~{fragments/sidebar :: sidebar}"></div>

    <div class="main-content">

        <div class="error-card">

            <div class="error-icon">🌙</div>

            <h1 class="error-title">
                Oopsie, something went wonky
            </h1>

            <div class="error-code">
                Error <span th:text="${status}">500</span>
            </div>

            <p class="error-message">
                Something unexpected happened.
            </p>

            <a class="primary-btn"
               th:href="@{/home}">
                Take me home
            </a>

        </div>

    </div>

</div>

</body>

That keeps the purple header, sidebar, and overall Prompt Vault branding instead of dropping users onto what feels like a completely separate page. For an internal business app, that usually feels much more polished.

HTML

<div class="category-list">

    <div class="category-row"
         th:each="category : ${categories}">

        <div class="category-name"
             th:text="${category.name}">
        </div>

        <div class="category-actions">

            <a class="secondary-btn"
               th:href="@{/admin/categories/{id}/edit(id=${category.id})}">
                Edit
            </a>

            <form th:action="@{/admin/categories/{id}/delete(id=${category.id})}"
                  method="post">

                <input type="hidden"
                       th:name="${_csrf.parameterName}"
                       th:value="${_csrf.token}" />

                <button type="submit"
                        class="danger-btn">
                    Delete
                </button>

            </form>

        </div>

    </div>

</div>

The easiest solution is to wrap both buttons in a flex container and make them each take 50% width.

}

with a nice 15px gap between them and both buttons taking equal width. This tends to look much more balanced on edit forms.

Prompt(2).java
File
If a prompt is linked to a category and the category is deleted, what happens to the prompt? There's a foreign key relation as you can see in my prompt.java

In your current Prompt entity, each prompt has:

@ManyToOne
@JoinColumn(name = "fk_category_id")
private PromptCategory category;

So many prompts can point to one category through fk_category_id.

With the mapping as it is now, deleting a category that is already linked to prompts will usually fail with a database foreign key constraint error.

So this:

repository.deleteById(id);

will likely throw an exception if any Prompt rows still reference that category.

The safest behaviour for your app is probably:

    Do not allow category deletion while prompts are using it.

Add this to a PromptRepository:

boolean existsByCategoryId(Long categoryId);

Then update your delete logic:

@Override
@Transactional
public void delete(Long id) {
    if (promptRepository.existsByCategoryId(id)) {
        throw new IllegalStateException(
                "Cannot delete category because it is assigned to one or more prompts"
        );
    }

    repository.deleteById(id);
}

Your PromptCategoryServiceImpl would then inject both repositories:

private final PromptCategoryRepository categoryRepository;
private final PromptRepository promptRepository;

I would not use cascade delete here. Deleting a category should not delete prompts. That would be risky data loss.

First, what model are you? I am building a springboot web-app with a mysql database and a thymeleaf front-end.

You just build a PromptCategory management page for me. I need similar for the FlaggedKeyword page. Only admins can view this page. Sanitisation of input should occur. You uploaded PolicyKeyword, mapped to policy_keywords, with a text field.

Use this structure:

// PolicyKeywordRepository.java
public interface PolicyKeywordRepository extends JpaRepository<PolicyKeyword, Long> {
    boolean existsByTextIgnoreCase(String text);
}

// PolicyKeywordService.java
@Service
public class PolicyKeywordService {

    private final PolicyKeywordRepository keywordRepo;
    private final PromptRepository promptRepo;

    public PolicyKeywordService(PolicyKeywordRepository keywordRepo, PromptRepository promptRepo) {
        this.keywordRepo = keywordRepo;
        this.promptRepo = promptRepo;
    }

    public List<PolicyKeyword> findAll() {
        return keywordRepo.findAll(Sort.by("text"));
    }

    public PolicyKeyword save(PolicyKeyword keyword) {
        String cleaned = HtmlUtils.htmlEscape(keyword.getText().trim());

        if (cleaned.isBlank()) {
            throw new IllegalArgumentException("Keyword cannot be blank");
        }

        keyword.setText(cleaned);
        return keywordRepo.save(keyword);
    }

    public void delete(Long id) {
        PolicyKeyword keyword = keywordRepo.findById(id)
            .orElseThrow(() -> new IllegalArgumentException("Keyword not found"));

        promptRepo.markPromptsAsNotFlaggedForKeyword(keyword.getText());
        keywordRepo.delete(keyword);
    }
}

// PromptRepository.java
@Modifying
@Transactional
@Query("UPDATE Prompt p SET p.flagged = false WHERE p.flagReason = :keyword")
void markPromptsAsNotFlaggedForKeyword(@Param("keyword") String keyword);

Adjust flagReason to whatever field stores the matching policy keyword.

// PolicyKeywordController.java
@Controller
@RequestMapping("/policy-keywords")
public class PolicyKeywordController {

    private final PolicyKeywordService service;

    public PolicyKeywordController(PolicyKeywordService service) {
        this.service = service;
    }

    @PreAuthorize("hasAnyRole('USER', 'ADMIN')")
    @GetMapping
    public String index(Model model) {
        model.addAttribute("keywords", service.findAll());
        model.addAttribute("policyKeyword", new PolicyKeyword());
        return "policy-keywords/index";
    }

    @PreAuthorize("hasRole('ADMIN')")
    @PostMapping
    public String create(@ModelAttribute PolicyKeyword policyKeyword) {
        service.save(policyKeyword);
        return "redirect:/policy-keywords";
    }

    @PreAuthorize("hasRole('ADMIN')")
    @PostMapping("/{id}")
    public String update(@PathVariable Long id, @ModelAttribute PolicyKeyword policyKeyword) {
        policyKeyword.setId(id);
        service.save(policyKeyword);
        return "redirect:/policy-keywords";
    }

    @PreAuthorize("hasRole('ADMIN')")
    @PostMapping("/{id}/delete")
    public String delete(@PathVariable Long id) {
        service.delete(id);
        return "redirect:/policy-keywords";
    }
}

FlaggedPrompt(1).java
File
Not quite - there's a join table for prompt <-> PolicyKeyword called FlaggedPrompt where when a prompt is saved we'll check against the keywords and make a record for this many to many relationship.
Also we'll want a PolicyKeywordService interface and a PolicyKeywordServiceImpl

Got it — the delete behaviour should remove the keyword relationship from FlaggedPrompt, not update a boolean on Prompt. I’ll align this with your Prompt and FlaggedPrompt models and split the service into interface plus implementation.

Yes — with your current models, Prompt has no flagged boolean, and FlaggedPrompt owns the link between a prompt and many PolicyKeywords.

Use this instead.

public interface PolicyKeywordService {
    List<PolicyKeyword> findAll();
    PolicyKeyword findById(Long id);
    PolicyKeyword save(PolicyKeyword policyKeyword);
    void deleteById(Long id);
}

@Service
public class PolicyKeywordServiceImpl implements PolicyKeywordService {

    private final PolicyKeywordRepository policyKeywordRepository;
    private final FlaggedPromptRepository flaggedPromptRepository;

    public PolicyKeywordServiceImpl(
            PolicyKeywordRepository policyKeywordRepository,
            FlaggedPromptRepository flaggedPromptRepository
    ) {
        this.policyKeywordRepository = policyKeywordRepository;
        this.flaggedPromptRepository = flaggedPromptRepository;
    }

    @Override
    public List<PolicyKeyword> findAll() {
        return policyKeywordRepository.findAll(Sort.by("text"));
    }

    @Override
    public PolicyKeyword findById(Long id) {
        return policyKeywordRepository.findById(id)
                .orElseThrow(() -> new IllegalArgumentException("Policy keyword not found"));
    }

    @Override
    public PolicyKeyword save(PolicyKeyword policyKeyword) {
        String cleaned = policyKeyword.getText() == null
                ? ""
                : policyKeyword.getText().trim();

        cleaned = HtmlUtils.htmlEscape(cleaned);

        if (cleaned.isBlank()) {
            throw new IllegalArgumentException("Keyword cannot be blank");
        }

        policyKeyword.setText(cleaned);
        return policyKeywordRepository.save(policyKeyword);
    }

    @Override
    @Transactional
    public void deleteById(Long id) {
        PolicyKeyword keyword = findById(id);

        List<FlaggedPrompt> flaggedPrompts =
                flaggedPromptRepository.findAllByKeywordsContaining(keyword);

        for (FlaggedPrompt flaggedPrompt : flaggedPrompts) {
            flaggedPrompt.getKeywords().remove(keyword);

            if (flaggedPrompt.getKeywords().isEmpty()) {
                flaggedPromptRepository.delete(flaggedPrompt);
            } else {
                flaggedPromptRepository.save(flaggedPrompt);
            }
        }

        policyKeywordRepository.delete(keyword);
    }
}

Repository:

public interface PolicyKeywordRepository extends JpaRepository<PolicyKeyword, Long> {
    boolean existsByTextIgnoreCase(String text);
}

public interface FlaggedPromptRepository extends JpaRepository<FlaggedPrompt, Long> {
    List<FlaggedPrompt> findAllByKeywordsContaining(PolicyKeyword keyword);
}

Controller:

@Controller
@RequestMapping("/policy-keywords")
public class PolicyKeywordController {

    private final PolicyKeywordService policyKeywordService;

    public PolicyKeywordController(PolicyKeywordService policyKeywordService) {
        this.policyKeywordService = policyKeywordService;
    }

    @PreAuthorize("hasAnyRole('USER', 'ADMIN')")
    @GetMapping
    public String index(Model model) {
        model.addAttribute("policyKeywords", policyKeywordService.findAll());
        model.addAttribute("policyKeyword", new PolicyKeyword());
        return "policy-keywords/index";
    }

    @PreAuthorize("hasRole('ADMIN')")
    @PostMapping("/add")
    public String add(@ModelAttribute PolicyKeyword policyKeyword) {
        policyKeywordService.save(policyKeyword);
        return "redirect:/policy-keywords";
    }

    @PreAuthorize("hasRole('ADMIN')")
    @PostMapping("/{id}/edit")
    public String edit(@PathVariable Long id, @ModelAttribute PolicyKeyword policyKeyword) {
        policyKeyword.setId(id);
        policyKeywordService.save(policyKeyword);
        return "redirect:/policy-keywords";
    }

    @PreAuthorize("hasRole('ADMIN')")
    @PostMapping("/{id}/delete")
    public String delete(@PathVariable Long id) {
        policyKeywordService.deleteById(id);
        return "redirect:/policy-keywords";
    }
}

Security:

.requestMatchers(HttpMethod.GET, "/policy-keywords").hasAnyRole("USER", "ADMIN")
.requestMatchers("/policy-keywords/**").hasRole("ADMIN")

The key point: deleting a PolicyKeyword removes it from each FlaggedPrompt.keywords; if that leaves the FlaggedPrompt with no keywords, the FlaggedPrompt record is deleted, making the accompanying prompt effectively “not flagged” anymore.

We also have an input sanitiser already:
package me.winterbelle.prompvault.utils.helpers.security;

import org.jsoup.Jsoup;
import org.jsoup.safety.Safelist;
import org.springframework.stereotype.Component;

@Component
public class InputSanitizer {

    public String sanitizePlainText(String input) {
        if (input == null) {
            return null;
        }

        return Jsoup.clean(input, Safelist.none()).trim();
    }
}

Perfect — then replace HtmlUtils.htmlEscape(...) with your existing helper:

private final InputSanitizer inputSanitizer;

public PolicyKeywordServiceImpl(
        PolicyKeywordRepository policyKeywordRepository,
        FlaggedPromptRepository flaggedPromptRepository,
        InputSanitizer inputSanitizer
) {
    this.policyKeywordRepository = policyKeywordRepository;
    this.flaggedPromptRepository = flaggedPromptRepository;
    this.inputSanitizer = inputSanitizer;
}

Then in save:

@Override
public PolicyKeyword save(PolicyKeyword policyKeyword) {
    String cleaned = inputSanitizer.sanitizePlainText(policyKeyword.getText());

    if (cleaned == null || cleaned.isBlank()) {
        throw new IllegalArgumentException("Keyword cannot be blank");
    }

    policyKeyword.setText(cleaned);
    return policyKeywordRepository.save(policyKeyword);
}

So the service should import:

import me.winterbelle.prompvault.utils.helpers.security.InputSanitizer;

This is better than escaping here, because your app already centralises sanitisation and uses Jsoup.clean(input, Safelist.none()).trim().

public record PolicyKeywordDto(
        @NotBlank(message = "Keyword is required")
        @Size(max = 255, message = "Keyword must be 255 characters or fewer")
        String text

Controller pattern matching your categories controller:

@Controller
@RequestMapping("/admin/policy-keywords")
@PreAuthorize("hasRole('ADMIN')")
public class AdminPolicyKeywordController {

    private final PolicyKeywordService service;

    public AdminPolicyKeywordController(PolicyKeywordService service) {
        this.service = service;
    }

    @GetMapping
    public String index(Model model) {
        model.addAttribute("keywords", service.findAll());
        return "admin/policy-keywords/index";
    }

    @GetMapping("/add")
    public String add(Model model) {
        model.addAttribute("keyword", new PolicyKeywordDto(""));
        return "admin/policy-keywords/add";
    }

    @PostMapping("/add")
    public String create(
            @Valid @ModelAttribute("keyword") PolicyKeywordDto dto,
            BindingResult bindingResult) {

        if (bindingResult.hasErrors()) {
            return "admin/policy-keywords/add";
        }

        service.create(dto);
        return "redirect:/admin/policy-keywords";
    }

    @GetMapping("/{id}/edit")
    public String edit(@PathVariable Long id, Model model) {
        var keyword = service.findById(id);

        model.addAttribute("keywordId", id);
        model.addAttribute("keyword", new PolicyKeywordDto(keyword.getText()));

        return "admin/policy-keywords/edit";
    }

    @PostMapping("/{id}/edit")
    public String update(
            @PathVariable Long id,
            @Valid @ModelAttribute("keyword") PolicyKeywordDto dto,
            BindingResult bindingResult) {

        if (bindingResult.hasErrors()) {
            return "admin/policy-keywords/edit";
        }

        service.update(id, dto);
        return "redirect:/admin/policy-keywords";
    }

    @PostMapping("/{id}/delete")
    public String delete(@PathVariable Long id) {
        service.deleteById(id);
        return "redirect:/admin/policy-keywords";
    }
}

Then the service interface becomes:

public interface PolicyKeywordService {
    List<PolicyKeyword> findAll();
    PolicyKeyword findById(Long id);
    PolicyKeyword create(PolicyKeywordDto dto);
    PolicyKeyword update(Long id, PolicyKeywordDto dto);
    void deleteById(Long id);
}

And in PolicyKeywordServiceImpl:

@Override
public PolicyKeyword create(PolicyKeywordDto dto) {
    PolicyKeyword keyword = new PolicyKeyword();
    keyword.setText(sanitizeKeyword(dto.text()));
    return policyKeywordRepository.save(keyword);
}

@Override
public PolicyKeyword update(Long id, PolicyKeywordDto dto) {
    PolicyKeyword keyword = findById(id);
    keyword.setText(sanitizeKeyword(dto.text()));
    return policyKeywordRepository.save(keyword);
}

private String sanitizeKeyword(String text) {
    String cleaned = inputSanitizer.sanitizePlainText(text);

    if (cleaned == null || cleaned.isBlank()) {
        throw new IllegalArgumentException("Keyword cannot be blank");
    }

    return cleaned;
}

Security config:

.requestMatchers("/admin/policy-keywords/**").hasRole("ADMIN")

This keeps it consistent with AdminPromptCategoryController, avoids manually setting inherited IDs, and keeps entity mutation inside the service.

<body>

    <div class="page-header">
        <h1>Policy Keywords</h1>

        <a th:href="@{/admin/policy-keywords/add}"
           class="btn btn-primary">
            Add Keyword
        </a>
    </div>

    <div class="card">
        <table class="admin-table">
            <thead>
            <tr>
                <th>Keyword</th>
                <th>Created</th>
                <th class="actions-column">Actions</th>
            </tr>
            </thead>

            <tbody>
            <tr th:each="keyword : ${keywords}">
                <td th:text="${keyword.text}"></td>

                <td th:text="${#temporals.format(keyword.createdDate, 'dd MMM yyyy')}">
                </td>

                <td>
                    <div class="action-buttons">

                        <a th:href="@{/admin/policy-keywords/{id}/edit(id=${keyword.id})}"
                           class="btn btn-secondary">
                            Edit
                        </a>

                        <form th:action="@{/admin/policy-keywords/{id}/delete(id=${keyword.id})}"
                              method="post"
                              onsubmit="return confirm('Delete this keyword?');">

                            <button type="submit"
                                    class="btn btn-danger">
                                Delete
                            </button>
                        </form>

                    </div>
                </td>
            </tr>

                <td colspan="3">
                    No policy keywords found.
                </td>
            </tr>
            </tbody>
        </table>
    </div>

</div>

One thing I'd also add for this particular feature: a usage count column showing how many FlaggedPrompts currently reference each keyword. Admins will immediately see whether deleting a keyword will unflag 2 prompts or 2,000 prompts, which is useful for moderation tooling.

Can't add/edit be the same?

Yes. For something as simple as a single text field, I'd probably use one form page and reuse it for both create and edit.

Controller:

@GetMapping("/add")
public String add(Model model) {
    model.addAttribute("keywordId", null);
    model.addAttribute("keyword", new PolicyKeywordDto(""));
    return "admin/policy-keywords/form";
}

@GetMapping("/{id}/edit")
public String edit(@PathVariable Long id, Model model) {
    var keyword = service.findById(id);

    model.addAttribute("keywordId", id);
    model.addAttribute("keyword", new PolicyKeywordDto(keyword.getText()));

    return "admin/policy-keywords/form";
}

Single template:

<h1 th:text="${keywordId == null ? 'Add Policy Keyword' : 'Edit Policy Keyword'}"></h1>

<form th:action="${keywordId == null}
                    ? @{/admin/policy-keywords/add}
                    : @{/admin/policy-keywords/{id}/edit(id=${keywordId})}"
      th:object="${keyword}"
      method="post">

    <div class="form-group">
        <label for="text">Keyword</label>

        <input id="text"
               type="text"
               th:field="*{text}"
               maxlength="255">
    </div>

    <div class="validation-error"
         th:if="${#fields.hasErrors('text')}"
         th:errors="*{text}">
    </div>

    <div class="form-actions">
        <button type="submit" class="btn btn-primary"
                th:text="${keywordId == null ? 'Create' : 'Update'}">
        </button>

        <a th:href="@{/admin/policy-keywords}"
           class="btn btn-secondary">
            Cancel
        </a>
    </div>

</form>

You can also make the POST handlers return the same form when validation fails:

@PostMapping("/add")
public String create(
        @Valid @ModelAttribute("keyword") PolicyKeywordDto dto,
        BindingResult bindingResult,
        Model model) {

    if (bindingResult.hasErrors()) {
        model.addAttribute("keywordId", null);
        return "admin/policy-keywords/form";
    }

    service.create(dto);
    return "redirect:/admin/policy-keywords";
}

@PostMapping("/{id}/edit")
public String update(
        @PathVariable Long id,
        @Valid @ModelAttribute("keyword") PolicyKeywordDto dto,
        BindingResult bindingResult,
        Model model) {

    if (bindingResult.hasErrors()) {
        model.addAttribute("keywordId", id);
        return "admin/policy-keywords/form";
    }

    service.update(id, dto);
    return "redirect:/admin/policy-keywords";
}

That's the pattern I'd use unless your category pages are already established as separate add/edit views and you want consistency across the admin area. For a single-field entity, one shared form.html is usually the cleanest option.

My security config:
package me.winterbelle.prompvault.utils.helpers.configs;

import me.winterbelle.prompvault.utils.helpers.auth.PromptVaultUserDetailsService;
import org.springframework.context.annotation.Bean;
import org.springframework.context.annotation.Configuration;
import org.springframework.security.authentication.AuthenticationProvider;
import org.springframework.security.authentication.dao.DaoAuthenticationProvider;
import org.springframework.security.config.annotation.method.configuration.EnableMethodSecurity;
import org.springframework.security.config.annotation.web.builders.HttpSecurity;
import org.springframework.security.config.annotation.web.configuration.EnableWebSecurity;
import org.springframework.security.crypto.bcrypt.BCryptPasswordEncoder;
import org.springframework.security.crypto.password.PasswordEncoder;
import org.springframework.security.web.SecurityFilterChain;

@Configuration
@EnableWebSecurity
@EnableMethodSecurity
public class SecurityConfig {

    @Bean
    public PasswordEncoder encoder() {
        return new BCryptPasswordEncoder();
    }

    @Bean
    SecurityFilterChain securityFilterChain(HttpSecurity http) {
        return http
                .formLogin(httpForm -> {
                    httpForm.loginPage("/req/login").permitAll();
                    httpForm.loginProcessingUrl("/req/login");
                    httpForm.defaultSuccessUrl("/home", true);
                })
//                .exceptionHandling(exception -> {
//                    exception.accessDeniedHandler((request, response, accessDeniedException) -> {
//                        response.sendRedirect("/home");
//                    });
//                })
                .authorizeHttpRequests(registry -> {
                    registry.requestMatchers("/req/**", "/css/**", "/js/**").permitAll();
                    registry.requestMatchers("/admin/**").hasRole("ADMIN");
                    registry.anyRequest().authenticated();
                })
                .build();
    }

    @Bean
    public AuthenticationProvider authenticationProvider(PromptVaultUserDetailsService userDetailsService, PasswordEncoder passwordEncoder) {
        DaoAuthenticationProvider provider = new DaoAuthenticationProvider(userDetailsService);
        provider.setPasswordEncoder(passwordEncoder);
        return provider;
    }
}

Why is visitng http://localhost:8080/admin/policy-keywords on my non-admin user showing the error page with 403 instead of redirecting to the home page like the prompt-category section?

Because your redirect handler is currently commented out:

// .exceptionHandling(exception -> {
//     exception.accessDeniedHandler((request, response, accessDeniedException) -> {
//         response.sendRedirect("/home");
//     });
// })

With this line active:

registry.requestMatchers("/admin/**").hasRole("ADMIN");

Spring correctly returns 403 Forbidden for authenticated non-admin users.

Re-enable the exception handler:

.exceptionHandling(exception -> {
    exception.accessDeniedHandler((request, response, accessDeniedException) -> {
        response.sendRedirect("/home");
    });
})

Full placement:

return http
        .formLogin(httpForm -> {
            httpForm.loginPage("/req/login").permitAll();
            httpForm.loginProcessingUrl("/req/login");
            httpForm.defaultSuccessUrl("/home", true);
        })
        .exceptionHandling(exception -> {
            exception.accessDeniedHandler((request, response, accessDeniedException) -> {
                response.sendRedirect("/home");
            });
        })
        .authorizeHttpRequests(registry -> {
            registry.requestMatchers("/req/**", "/css/**", "/js/**").permitAll();
            registry.requestMatchers("/admin/**").hasRole("ADMIN");
            registry.anyRequest().authenticated();
        })
        .build();

The prompt-category section likely redirected before because that handler was enabled at the time, or because the sidebar/link/controller path didn’t hit /admin/** in the same way.

The nice thing is that once you have:

.admin-list
.admin-row
.admin-name
.admin-actions

you can reuse them for:

    Prompt Categories

    Policy Keywords

    User Management

    Roles

    Prompt Reports

    Flagged Prompts

without creating another set of almost-identical CSS classes every time. That's usually the point where it's worth generalising the naming.

I can create multiple policy keywords with the exact same text. That shouldn't happen. It should be case insensitive too so Text and teXt are identical

I'd enforce this in three places:
1. Service layer (required)

Normalize and check before saving.

private String sanitizeKeyword(String text) {
    String cleaned = inputSanitizer.sanitizePlainText(text);

    if (cleaned == null || cleaned.isBlank()) {
        throw new IllegalArgumentException("Keyword cannot be blank");
    }

    return cleaned.trim();
}

Create:

@Override
public PolicyKeyword create(PolicyKeywordDto dto) {

    String keywordText = sanitizeKeyword(dto.text());

    if (policyKeywordRepository.existsByTextIgnoreCase(keywordText)) {
        throw new IllegalArgumentException("Policy keyword already exists");
    }

    PolicyKeyword keyword = new PolicyKeyword();
    keyword.setText(keywordText);

    return policyKeywordRepository.save(keyword);
}

Update:

@Override
public PolicyKeyword update(Long id, PolicyKeywordDto dto) {

    PolicyKeyword keyword = findById(id);

    String keywordText = sanitizeKeyword(dto.text());

    policyKeywordRepository.findByTextIgnoreCase(keywordText)
            .filter(existing -> !existing.getId().equals(id))
            .ifPresent(existing -> {
                throw new IllegalArgumentException("Policy keyword already exists");
            });

    keyword.setText(keywordText);

    return policyKeywordRepository.save(keyword);
}

Repository:

boolean existsByTextIgnoreCase(String text);

Optional<PolicyKeyword> findByTextIgnoreCase(String text);

2. Database unique constraint (strongly recommended)

Application validation alone is not enough.

If two admins submit at the same time you can still get duplicates.
Best approach

Store a normalized value.

@Column(nullable = false)
private String text;

@Column(nullable = false, unique = true)
private String normalizedText;

Example:
text	normalizedText
Text	text
teXt	text
TEXT	text

Then:

keyword.setText(keywordText);
keyword.setNormalizedText(keywordText.toLowerCase(Locale.ROOT));

and put a unique index on normalized_text.

This is the most reliable solution.
3. Show validation error on the form

Instead of throwing an exception into a 500 page:

try {
    service.create(dto);
} catch (IllegalArgumentException ex) {
    bindingResult.rejectValue(
            "text",
            "duplicate",
            ex.getMessage()
    );

    model.addAttribute("keywordId", null);

    return "admin/policy-keywords/form";
}

Then the user sees:

Policy keyword already exists

under the textbox.

For your project specifically, I'd add:

@Column(nullable = false, unique = true)
private String normalizedText;

to PolicyKeyword.

Relying solely on existsByTextIgnoreCase(...) is fine for a hobby project, but the database should ultimately enforce uniqueness because that's the source of truth.

Do I need findByTextIgnoreCase or can i just use existsByTextIngoreCase?

You can use only existsByTextIgnoreCase(...) for create, but for update it becomes awkward.

For example:

Current record:

ID=5
text="OpenAI"

User edits it and saves:

ID=5
text="OpenAI"

If you do:

if (policyKeywordRepository.existsByTextIgnoreCase(keywordText)) {
    throw new IllegalArgumentException("Policy keyword already exists");
}

then the update will fail because it finds itself.

That's why people often use:

Optional<PolicyKeyword> findByTextIgnoreCase(String text);

and then:

var existing = repository.findByTextIgnoreCase(keywordText);

if (existing.isPresent() && !existing.get().getId().equals(id)) {
    throw new IllegalArgumentException("Policy keyword already exists");
}

An alternative if you want to avoid findByTextIgnoreCase is a custom exists query:

boolean existsByTextIgnoreCaseAndIdNot(String text, Long id);

Then update becomes:

if (repository.existsByTextIgnoreCaseAndIdNot(keywordText, id)) {
    throw new IllegalArgumentException("Policy keyword already exists");
}

Personally I'd use:

boolean existsByTextIgnoreCase(String text);

boolean existsByTextIgnoreCaseAndIdNot(String text, Long id);

because they're very readable and you never need to load an entity just to perform a uniqueness check. This is probably the cleanest Spring Data approach for your use case.

ok show me that approach and the front end piece too

Use this repository approach:

public interface PolicyKeywordRepository extends JpaRepository<PolicyKeyword, Long> {

    boolean existsByTextIgnoreCase(String text);

    boolean existsByTextIgnoreCaseAndIdNot(String text, Long id);
}

Service:

@Override
public PolicyKeyword create(PolicyKeywordDto dto) {
    String keywordText = sanitizeKeyword(dto.text());

    if (policyKeywordRepository.existsByTextIgnoreCase(keywordText)) {
        throw new IllegalArgumentException("Policy keyword already exists");
    }

    PolicyKeyword keyword = new PolicyKeyword();
    keyword.setText(keywordText);

    return policyKeywordRepository.save(keyword);
}

@Override
public PolicyKeyword update(Long id, PolicyKeywordDto dto) {
    PolicyKeyword keyword = findById(id);

    String keywordText = sanitizeKeyword(dto.text());

    if (policyKeywordRepository.existsByTextIgnoreCaseAndIdNot(keywordText, id)) {
        throw new IllegalArgumentException("Policy keyword already exists");
    }

    keyword.setText(keywordText);

    return policyKeywordRepository.save(keyword);
}

Controller front-end validation handling:

@PostMapping("/add")
public String create(
        @Valid @ModelAttribute("keyword") PolicyKeywordDto dto,
        BindingResult bindingResult,
        Model model) {

    if (bindingResult.hasErrors()) {
        model.addAttribute("keywordId", null);
        return "admin/policy-keywords/form";
    }

    try {
        service.create(dto);
    } catch (IllegalArgumentException ex) {
        bindingResult.rejectValue("text", "duplicate", ex.getMessage());
        model.addAttribute("keywordId", null);
        return "admin/policy-keywords/form";
    }

    return "redirect:/admin/policy-keywords";
}

@PostMapping("/{id}/edit")
public String update(
        @PathVariable Long id,
        @Valid @ModelAttribute("keyword") PolicyKeywordDto dto,
        BindingResult bindingResult,
        Model model) {

    if (bindingResult.hasErrors()) {
        model.addAttribute("keywordId", id);
        return "admin/policy-keywords/form";
    }

    try {
        service.update(id, dto);
    } catch (IllegalArgumentException ex) {
        bindingResult.rejectValue("text", "duplicate", ex.getMessage());
        model.addAttribute("keywordId", id);
        return "admin/policy-keywords/form";
    }

    return "redirect:/admin/policy-keywords";
}

Your form.html already supports this with:

<div class="validation-message error"
     th:if="${#fields.hasErrors('text')}"
     th:errors="*{text}">
</div>

So duplicate keywords will now show the error directly below the input.

do i still need the normalizedText on the model?

Not necessarily.

There are two separate concerns:
Option 1: Application-level uniqueness only

Keep:

boolean existsByTextIgnoreCase(String text);

boolean existsByTextIgnoreCaseAndIdNot(String text, Long id);

and don't add normalizedText.

Your entity stays:

@Entity
@Table(name = "policy_keywords")
public class PolicyKeyword extends AuditableEntity {

    private String text;

    // getters/setters
}

This is simple and perfectly fine for a small/internal application.
Option 2: Database-enforced case-insensitive uniqueness

If you want the database to guarantee:

Text
TEXT
teXt

can never coexist, then you need something extra because a normal unique constraint on text is case-sensitive in many database configurations.

That's where a field like:

@Column(nullable = false, unique = true)
private String normalizedText;

becomes useful.

You'd save:

text = "TeXt"
normalizedText = "text"

and put the unique constraint on normalizedText.
What I'd do for PromptVault

For now, don't add normalizedText.

Use:

existsByTextIgnoreCase(...)
existsByTextIgnoreCaseAndIdNot(...)

and keep the model simple.

Only introduce normalizedText if:

    you expect lots of concurrent admins,

    you want the database itself to enforce uniqueness,

    or you start seeing race-condition issues.

For a typical Spring Boot admin CRUD screen managed by a handful of admins, the repository checks are usually sufficient and much less code.

categories has this little card for quickly adding. Let's have that for keywords too

Yes — then don’t use /add as a separate page. Keep form.html only for edit, and make create happen directly from index.html.

Update index controller:

@GetMapping
public String index(Model model) {
    model.addAttribute("keywords", service.findAll());
    model.addAttribute("keyword", new PolicyKeywordDto(""));
    return "admin/policy-keywords/index";
}

Create handler validation should return index:

@PostMapping("/add")
public String create(
        @Valid @ModelAttribute("keyword") PolicyKeywordDto dto,
        BindingResult bindingResult,
        Model model) {

    if (bindingResult.hasErrors()) {
        model.addAttribute("keywords", service.findAll());
        return "admin/policy-keywords/index";
    }

    try {
        service.create(dto);
    } catch (IllegalArgumentException ex) {
        bindingResult.rejectValue("text", "duplicate", ex.getMessage());
        model.addAttribute("keywords", service.findAll());
        return "admin/policy-keywords/index";
    }

    return "redirect:/admin/policy-keywords";
}

               th:name="${_csrf.parameterName}"
               th:value="${_csrf.token}" />

        <div class="form-group">

            <input id="text"
                   type="text"
                   th:field="*{text}"
                   placeholder="Enter policy keyword" />

            <div class="validation-message error"
                 th:if="${#fields.hasErrors('text')}"
                 th:errors="*{text}">
            </div>

                class="primary-btn">
            Add Keyword
        </button>

    </form>

    <p class="admin-empty"
       th:if="${#lists.isEmpty(keywords)}">
        No policy keywords have been configured.
    </p>

    <div class="admin-row"
         th:each="policyKeyword : ${keywords}">

        <div class="admin-name"
             th:text="${policyKeyword.text}">
            Keyword
        </div>

        <div class="admin-actions">

            <a class="secondary-btn"
               th:href="@{/admin/policy-keywords/{id}/edit(id=${policyKeyword.id})}">
                Edit
            </a>

            <form th:action="@{/admin/policy-keywords/{id}/delete(id=${policyKeyword.id})}"
                  method="post"
                  onsubmit="return confirm('Delete this keyword? This may unflag prompts using only this keyword.');">

                <input type="hidden"
                       th:name="${_csrf.parameterName}"
                       th:value="${_csrf.token}" />

                <button type="submit"
                        class="danger-btn">
                    Delete
                </button>

            </form>

        </div>

    </div>

</div>

import java.util.List;

public interface PromptVaultUserService {

    Optional<PromptVaultUser> findUser(String username);

    Optional<PromptVaultUser> findUserByEmail(String email);

    Optional<PromptVaultUser> findUser(Long id);

}

3. Service implementation

import me.winterbelle.prompvault.utils.enums.Status;

import java.util.List;

@Override
public List<PromptVaultUser> findAllUsers() {
    return promptVaultUserRepository.findAll();
}

@Override
public void updateUserStatus(Long id, Status status) {
    PromptVaultUser user = promptVaultUserRepository.findById(id)
            .orElseThrow(() -> new IllegalArgumentException("User not found"));

    user.setStatus(status);
    promptVaultUserRepository.save(user);
}

4. Admin controller

package me.winterbelle.prompvault.controllers;

import me.winterbelle.prompvault.services.user.PromptVaultUserService;
import me.winterbelle.prompvault.utils.enums.Status;
import org.springframework.security.access.prepost.PreAuthorize;
import org.springframework.stereotype.Controller;
import org.springframework.ui.Model;
import org.springframework.web.bind.annotation.*;

@Controller
@RequestMapping("/admin/users")
@PreAuthorize("hasRole('ADMIN')")
public class AdminUserController {

    private final PromptVaultUserService userService;

    public AdminUserController(PromptVaultUserService userService) {
        this.userService = userService;
    }

    @GetMapping
    public String manageUsers(Model model) {
        model.addAttribute("users", userService.findAllUsers());
        return "admin/manage-users";
    }

    @PostMapping("/{id}/enable")
    public String enableUser(@PathVariable Long id) {
        userService.updateUserStatus(id, Status.ENABLED);
        return "redirect:/admin/users";
    }

    @PostMapping("/{id}/disable")
    public String disableUser(@PathVariable Long id) {
        userService.updateUserStatus(id, Status.DISABLED);
        return "redirect:/admin/users";
    }
}

Use your actual enum names if your Status enum is ACTIVE/INACTIVE instead of ENABLED/DISABLED.

this is missing a way to change the user status

Your buttons are not showing because the template checks uppercase enum values. Your app is rendering lowercase: enabled.

Change the th:if checks to lowercase:

<div class="admin-actions">

    <form th:if="${user.status.name() == 'disabled'}"
          th:action="@{/admin/users/{id}/enable(id=${user.id})}"
          method="post">

        <input type="hidden"
               th:name="${_csrf.parameterName}"
               th:value="${_csrf.token}" />

        <button type="submit"
                class="primary-btn">
            Enable
        </button>

    </form>

    <form th:if="${user.status.name() == 'enabled'}"
          th:action="@{/admin/users/{id}/disable(id=${user.id})}"
          method="post">

        <input type="hidden"
               th:name="${_csrf.parameterName}"
               th:value="${_csrf.token}" />

        <button type="submit"
                class="danger-btn">
            Disable
        </button>

    </form>

</div>

Or safer:

<form th:if="${user.status.toString() == 'disabled'}" ...>

and

<form th:if="${user.status.toString() == 'enabled'}" ...>

Since both users are currently enabled, each card should show a Disable button.

Here's another admin controller as an example. This FlaggedPromptController shoudl be AdminFlaggedPromptController and ensure non-admins can't see any of it

Yes, based on your example controller, I'd structure it similarly and protect the entire controller with @PreAuthorize("hasRole('ADMIN')") so non-admins cannot access any endpoint in it.

Assuming you have a FlaggedPromptService, something like this would fit your project's pattern:

package me.winterbelle.prompvault.controllers.admin;

import me.winterbelle.prompvault.services.flaggedprompt.FlaggedPromptService;
import org.springframework.security.access.prepost.PreAuthorize;
import org.springframework.stereotype.Controller;
import org.springframework.ui.Model;
import org.springframework.web.bind.annotation.GetMapping;
import org.springframework.web.bind.annotation.RequestMapping;

@Controller
@RequestMapping("/admin/flagged-prompts")
@PreAuthorize("hasRole('ADMIN')")
public class AdminFlaggedPromptController {

    private final FlaggedPromptService service;

    public AdminFlaggedPromptController(FlaggedPromptService service) {
        this.service = service;
    }

    @GetMapping
    public String index(Model model) {

        model.addAttribute("flaggedPrompts", service.findAll());

        return "admin/flagged-prompts/index";
    }
}

A corresponding service method might simply be:

public List<FlaggedPrompt> findAll() {
    return flaggedPromptRepository.findAll();
}

or, preferably, sorted newest first:

public List<FlaggedPrompt> findAll() {
    return flaggedPromptRepository.findAll(
        Sort.by(Sort.Direction.DESC, "createdDate")
    );
}

Since your requirements only mention viewing flagged prompts, the controller only needs the index() action. No add/edit/delete endpoints are necessary.

The security is handled by:

@PreAuthorize("hasRole('ADMIN')")

which matches the pattern used in your existing admin controller and prevents non-admin users from accessing any handler method in the controller.

One thing I'd recommend is creating a DTO/view model rather than exposing entities directly to the view. The page needs:

    Prompt title

    Prompt owner username

    Category name

    List of keyword texts

    FlaggedPrompt created date

Those values come from traversing FlaggedPrompt → Prompt → PromptVaultUser and PromptCategory, which can easily cause lazy-loading issues in Thymeleaf if the session is closed.

If you're already using DTOs elsewhere in the project, I'd follow the same approach here.

Show me the service, serviceImpl, repository, Dto.
Remmeber this FlaggedPrompt is a join table for Prompt <-> PolicyKeyword so we need to group by prompt and condense all keywords into one line

Yes — because one FlaggedPrompt represents one flagged prompt with many PolicyKeywords, the DTO should flatten it into one row/card per prompt, with keywords condensed into one string/list. Your model already has FlaggedPrompt -> Prompt and FlaggedPrompt -> List<PolicyKeyword>.
FlaggedPromptDto.java

package me.winterbelle.prompvault.models.dtos;

import java.time.LocalDateTime;

public class FlaggedPromptDto {

    private Long id;
    private String promptTitle;
    private String ownerUsername;
    private String categoryName;
    private String keywords;
    private LocalDateTime createdDate;

    public FlaggedPromptDto(
            Long id,
            String promptTitle,
            String ownerUsername,
            String categoryName,
            String keywords,
            LocalDateTime createdDate) {
        this.id = id;
        this.promptTitle = promptTitle;
        this.ownerUsername = ownerUsername;
        this.categoryName = categoryName;
        this.keywords = keywords;
        this.createdDate = createdDate;
    }

    public Long getId() {
        return id;
    }

    public String getPromptTitle() {
        return promptTitle;
    }

    public String getOwnerUsername() {
        return ownerUsername;
    }

    public String getCategoryName() {
        return categoryName;
    }

    public String getKeywords() {
        return keywords;
    }

    public LocalDateTime getCreatedDate() {
        return createdDate;
    }
}

FlaggedPromptRepository.java

package me.winterbelle.prompvault.models.repositories;

import me.winterbelle.prompvault.models.data.FlaggedPrompt;
import org.springframework.data.jpa.repository.EntityGraph;
import org.springframework.data.jpa.repository.JpaRepository;

import java.util.List;

public interface FlaggedPromptRepository extends JpaRepository<FlaggedPrompt, Long> {

    @EntityGraph(attributePaths = {
            "prompt",
            "prompt.account",
            "prompt.category",
            "keywords"
    })
    List<FlaggedPrompt> findAllByOrderByCreatedDateDesc();
}

FlaggedPromptService.java

package me.winterbelle.prompvault.services.flaggedprompt;

import me.winterbelle.prompvault.models.dtos.FlaggedPromptDto;

import java.util.List;

public interface FlaggedPromptService {

    List<FlaggedPromptDto> findAll();
}

FlaggedPromptServiceImpl.java

package me.winterbelle.prompvault.services.flaggedprompt;

import me.winterbelle.prompvault.models.data.FlaggedPrompt;
import me.winterbelle.prompvault.models.data.PolicyKeyword;
import me.winterbelle.prompvault.models.dtos.FlaggedPromptDto;
import me.winterbelle.prompvault.models.repositories.FlaggedPromptRepository;
import org.springframework.stereotype.Service;

import java.util.List;
import java.util.stream.Collectors;

@Service
public class FlaggedPromptServiceImpl implements FlaggedPromptService {

    private final FlaggedPromptRepository flaggedPromptRepository;

    public FlaggedPromptServiceImpl(FlaggedPromptRepository flaggedPromptRepository) {
        this.flaggedPromptRepository = flaggedPromptRepository;
    }

    @Override
    public List<FlaggedPromptDto> findAll() {
        return flaggedPromptRepository.findAllByOrderByCreatedDateDesc()
                .stream()
                .map(this::toDto)
                .toList();
    }

    private FlaggedPromptDto toDto(FlaggedPrompt flaggedPrompt) {

        String keywords = flaggedPrompt.getKeywords()
                .stream()
                .map(PolicyKeyword::getText)
                .distinct()
                .sorted()
                .collect(Collectors.joining(", "));

        return new FlaggedPromptDto(
                flaggedPrompt.getId(),
                flaggedPrompt.getPrompt().getTitle(),
                flaggedPrompt.getPrompt().getAccount().getUsername(),
                flaggedPrompt.getPrompt().getCategory().getName(),
                keywords,
                flaggedPrompt.getCreatedDate()
        );
    }
}

Then your controller uses the DTOs:

package me.winterbelle.prompvault.controllers.admin;

@PreAuthorize("hasRole('ADMIN')")
public class AdminFlaggedPromptController {

    private final FlaggedPromptService service;

    public AdminFlaggedPromptController(FlaggedPromptService service) {
        this.service = service;
    }

    @GetMapping
    public String index(Model model) {
        model.addAttribute("flaggedPrompts", service.findAll());
        return "admin/flagged-prompts/index";
    }
}

I don't think the promptcategoryservice has a get all categories method. I need that too. 
Here's the prompt and prompt category methods. You can decide if it's better to submit just the id when creating a prompt

Yes — for create prompt, it’s cleaner to submit categoryId, then fetch the PromptCategory in the controller/service. Your Prompt stores a full PromptCategory object, not just an id , and PromptCategory only has name because it inherits id from AuditableEntity .

Add this to PromptCategoryService:

List<PromptCategory> getAllCategories();

PromptCategory getCategory(Long id);

In PromptCategoryServiceImpl:

@Override
public List<PromptCategory> getAllCategories() {
    return promptCategoryRepository.findAll();
}

@Override
public PromptCategory getCategory(Long id) {
    return promptCategoryRepository.findById(id)
            .orElseThrow(() -> new RuntimeException("Category not found"));
}

Then use a DTO for creating prompts:

public class PromptCreateDto {

    private String title;
    private String promptText;
    private Long categoryId;
    private Visibility visibility;

    // getters and setters
}

Controller:

@GetMapping("/create")
public String showCreatePromptForm(Model model) {
    model.addAttribute("prompt", new PromptCreateDto());
    model.addAttribute("categories", promptCategoryService.getAllCategories());
    model.addAttribute("visibilities", Visibility.values());

    return "prompts/create";
}

@PostMapping("/create")
public String createPrompt(
        @ModelAttribute("prompt") PromptCreateDto promptDto,
        @SessionAttribute UserDetailsObject user,
        RedirectAttributes redirectAttributes) {

    PromptCategory category =
            promptCategoryService.getCategory(promptDto.getCategoryId());

    Prompt prompt = new Prompt();
    prompt.setTitle(promptDto.getTitle());
    prompt.setPromptText(promptDto.getPromptText());
    prompt.setCategory(category);
    prompt.setVisibility(promptDto.getVisibility());

    promptService.createPrompt(prompt);

    redirectAttributes.addFlashAttribute(
            "message",
            "Prompt created successfully");

    return "redirect:/prompts";
}

I get a 400 error and this is all the logs: 
Hibernate: select pc1_0.id,pc1_0.created_at,pc1_0.name,pc1_0.updated_at from prompt_categories pc1_0
2026-06-14T21:33:33.823+01:00  WARN 53042 --- [PrompVault] [nio-8080-exec-2] .w.s.m.s.DefaultHandlerExceptionResolver : Resolved [org.springframework.web.bind.ServletRequestBindingException: Missing session attribute 'user' of type UserDetailsObject]

Your 400 is from this parameter:

@SessionAttribute UserDetailsObject user

Spring is saying there is no session attribute named user, so the controller method fails before saving.

Use Spring Security’s authenticated user instead:

@PostMapping("/create")
public String createPrompt(
        @ModelAttribute("prompt") PromptCreateDto promptDto,
        @AuthenticationPrincipal UserDetailsObject user,
        RedirectAttributes redirectAttributes) {

    PromptCategory category =
            promptCategoryService.getCategory(promptDto.getCategoryId());

    Prompt prompt = new Prompt();
    prompt.setTitle(promptDto.getTitle());
    prompt.setPromptText(promptDto.getPromptText());
    prompt.setCategory(category);
    prompt.setVisibility(promptDto.getVisibility());

    promptService.createPromptForUser(prompt, user.getUserId());

    redirectAttributes.addFlashAttribute(
            "message",
            "Prompt created successfully");

    return "redirect:/prompts";
}

Add import:

import org.springframework.security.core.annotation.AuthenticationPrincipal;

Then update your PromptService so the service sets the owner/account:

Prompt createPromptForUser(Prompt prompt, Long userId);

In PromptServiceImpl:

@Override
public Prompt createPromptForUser(Prompt prompt, Long userId) {
    PromptVaultUser account = userRepository.findById(userId)
            .orElseThrow(() -> new RuntimeException("User not found"));

    prompt.setAccount(account);

    return promptRepository.save(prompt);
}

So the issue is not the category query — that part worked. The crash happens because @SessionAttribute user does not exist. Use @AuthenticationPrincipal instead.

Here's the security config:
package me.winterbelle.prompvault.utils.helpers.configs;

import me.winterbelle.prompvault.utils.helpers.auth.PromptVaultUserDetailsService;
import org.springframework.context.annotation.Bean;
import org.springframework.context.annotation.Configuration;
import org.springframework.security.authentication.AuthenticationProvider;
import org.springframework.security.authentication.dao.DaoAuthenticationProvider;
import org.springframework.security.config.annotation.method.configuration.EnableMethodSecurity;
import org.springframework.security.config.annotation.web.builders.HttpSecurity;
import org.springframework.security.config.annotation.web.configuration.EnableWebSecurity;
import org.springframework.security.crypto.bcrypt.BCryptPasswordEncoder;
import org.springframework.security.crypto.password.PasswordEncoder;
import org.springframework.security.web.SecurityFilterChain;

@Configuration
@EnableWebSecurity
@EnableMethodSecurity
public class SecurityConfig {

    @Bean
    public PasswordEncoder encoder() {
        return new BCryptPasswordEncoder();
    }

    @Bean
    SecurityFilterChain securityFilterChain(HttpSecurity http) {
        return http
                .formLogin(httpForm -> {
                    httpForm.loginPage("/req/login").permitAll();
                    httpForm.loginProcessingUrl("/req/login");
                    httpForm.defaultSuccessUrl("/home", true);
                })
                .exceptionHandling(exception -> {
                    exception.accessDeniedHandler((request, response, accessDeniedException) -> {
                        response.sendRedirect("/home");
                    });
                })
                .authorizeHttpRequests(registry -> {
                    registry.requestMatchers("/req/**", "/css/**", "/js/**").permitAll();
                    registry.requestMatchers("/admin/**").hasRole("ADMIN");
                    registry.anyRequest().authenticated();
                })
                .build();
    }

    @Bean
    public AuthenticationProvider authenticationProvider(PromptVaultUserDetailsService userDetailsService, PasswordEncoder passwordEncoder) {
        DaoAuthenticationProvider provider = new DaoAuthenticationProvider(userDetailsService);
        provider.setPasswordEncoder(passwordEncoder);
        return provider;
    }
}

I think we can use the Authentication authetncation concern for the method, right?

Yes, you can use Authentication authentication here.

That is probably the neatest fix with your current setup:

@PostMapping("/create")
public String createPrompt(
        @ModelAttribute("prompt") PromptCreateDto promptDto,
        Authentication authentication,
        RedirectAttributes redirectAttributes) {

    UserDetailsObject user =
            (UserDetailsObject) authentication.getPrincipal();

    PromptCategory category =
            promptCategoryService.getCategory(promptDto.getCategoryId());

    Prompt prompt = new Prompt();
    prompt.setTitle(promptDto.getTitle());
    prompt.setPromptText(promptDto.getPromptText());
    prompt.setCategory(category);
    prompt.setVisibility(promptDto.getVisibility());

    promptService.createPromptForUser(prompt, user.getUserId());

    redirectAttributes.addFlashAttribute(
            "message",
            "Prompt created successfully");

    return "redirect:/prompts";
}

Import:

import org.springframework.security.core.Authentication;

And update your GET list method too, because this can cause the same issue:

@GetMapping
public String listPrompts(
        Authentication authentication,
        Model model) {

    UserDetailsObject user =
            (UserDetailsObject) authentication.getPrincipal();

    model.addAttribute(
            "prompts",
            promptService.getPromptsForUser(user.getUserId()));

    return "prompts/list";
}

So yes: replace @SessionAttribute UserDetailsObject user with Authentication authentication, then cast authentication.getPrincipal() to your UserDetailsObject.

the prompt service does not need the userId, right?

Correct. If you're already constructing the Prompt in the controller, the service doesn't necessarily need a userId.

The important thing is that before saving, the Prompt.account field is populated because it's a @ManyToOne relationship on the entity.

You have two common approaches:
Option 1 (my preference): Service receives a fully populated Prompt

Controller:

UserDetailsObject user =
        (UserDetailsObject) authentication.getPrincipal();

PromptVaultUser account =
        userService.getUser(user.getUserId());

Prompt prompt = new Prompt();
prompt.setTitle(promptDto.getTitle());
prompt.setPromptText(promptDto.getPromptText());
prompt.setCategory(category);
prompt.setVisibility(promptDto.getVisibility());
prompt.setAccount(account);

promptService.createPrompt(prompt);

Service:

@Override
public Prompt createPrompt(Prompt prompt) {
    return promptRepository.save(prompt);
}

This keeps the service simple.
Option 2: Service handles user lookup

Controller:

promptService.createPrompt(
        promptDto,
        user.getUserId());

Service:

public Prompt createPrompt(
        PromptCreateDto dto,
        Long userId) {

    // lookup user
    // lookup category
    // build prompt
    // save
}

This moves more business logic into the service.

For your current project structure, I'd lean toward Option 1 because your PromptService already exposes:

Prompt createPrompt(Prompt prompt);

so there's no need to change the service signature. Just make sure the controller sets:

prompt.setAccount(account);

before calling:

promptService.createPrompt(prompt);

Otherwise Hibernate will save a prompt with a null owner (or fail if the FK is non-nullable).

give me the whole prompt controller including the previous methods

package me.winterbelle.prompvault.controllers;

import me.winterbelle.prompvault.dtos.PromptCreateDto;
import me.winterbelle.prompvault.models.data.Prompt;
import me.winterbelle.prompvault.models.data.PromptCategory;
import me.winterbelle.prompvault.models.data.PromptHistoryItem;
import me.winterbelle.prompvault.models.data.PromptVaultUser;
import me.winterbelle.prompvault.services.categories.PromptCategoryService;
import me.winterbelle.prompvault.services.prompts.PromptService;
import me.winterbelle.prompvault.services.users.UserService;
import me.winterbelle.prompvault.utils.enums.Visibility;
import me.winterbelle.prompvault.utils.helpers.auth.UserDetailsObject;
import org.springframework.security.core.Authentication;
import org.springframework.stereotype.Controller;
import org.springframework.ui.Model;
import org.springframework.web.bind.annotation.*;
import org.springframework.web.servlet.mvc.support.RedirectAttributes;

@Controller
@RequestMapping("/prompts")
public class PromptController {

    private final PromptService promptService;
    private final PromptCategoryService promptCategoryService;
    private final UserService userService;

    public PromptController(
            PromptService promptService,
            PromptCategoryService promptCategoryService,
            UserService userService) {
        this.promptService = promptService;
        this.promptCategoryService = promptCategoryService;
        this.userService = userService;
    }

    @GetMapping
    public String listPrompts(
            Authentication authentication,
            Model model) {

        UserDetailsObject user =
                (UserDetailsObject) authentication.getPrincipal();

        model.addAttribute(
                "prompts",
                promptService.getPromptsForUser(user.getUserId()));

        return "prompts/list";
    }

    @GetMapping("/create")
    public String showCreatePromptForm(Model model) {

        model.addAttribute("prompt", new PromptCreateDto());
        model.addAttribute("categories", promptCategoryService.getAllCategories());
        model.addAttribute("visibilities", Visibility.values());

        return "prompts/create";
    }

    @PostMapping("/create")
    public String createPrompt(
            @ModelAttribute("prompt") PromptCreateDto promptDto,
            Authentication authentication,
            RedirectAttributes redirectAttributes) {

        UserDetailsObject user =
                (UserDetailsObject) authentication.getPrincipal();

        PromptVaultUser account =
                userService.getUser(user.getUserId());

        PromptCategory category =
                promptCategoryService.getCategory(promptDto.getCategoryId());

        Prompt prompt = new Prompt();
        prompt.setTitle(promptDto.getTitle());
        prompt.setPromptText(promptDto.getPromptText());
        prompt.setCategory(category);
        prompt.setVisibility(promptDto.getVisibility());
        prompt.setAccount(account);

        promptService.createPrompt(prompt);

        redirectAttributes.addFlashAttribute(
                "message",
                "Prompt created successfully");

        return "redirect:/prompts";
    }

    @PostMapping("/send/{id}")
    public String sendPrompt(
            @PathVariable Long id,
            RedirectAttributes redirectAttributes) {

        PromptHistoryItem result =
                promptService.sendPrompt(id);

        redirectAttributes.addFlashAttribute(
                "message",
                result.getResponseText());

        return "redirect:/prompts";
    }
}

You may need to adjust these imports/package names depending on your actual folders:

import me.winterbelle.prompvault.dtos.PromptCreateDto;
import me.winterbelle.prompvault.services.categories.PromptCategoryService;
import me.winterbelle.prompvault.services.users.UserService;

Yep — your service has:

PromptVaultUser account =

public PromptController(

        PromptCategoryService promptCategoryService,
        PromptVaultUserService promptVaultUserService) {

    this.promptCategoryService = promptCategoryService;

Your create method should use:

@PostMapping("/create")
public String createPrompt(
        @ModelAttribute("prompt") PromptCreateDto promptDto,
        Authentication authentication,
        RedirectAttributes redirectAttributes) {

    UserDetailsObject user =
            (UserDetailsObject) authentication.getPrincipal();

    PromptVaultUser account =
            promptVaultUserService.findUser(user.getUserId())
                    .orElseThrow(() -> new IllegalArgumentException("User not found"));

    PromptCategory category =
            promptCategoryService.getCategory(promptDto.getCategoryId());

    Prompt prompt = new Prompt();
    prompt.setTitle(promptDto.getTitle());
    prompt.setPromptText(promptDto.getPromptText());
    prompt.setCategory(category);
    prompt.setVisibility(promptDto.getVisibility());
    prompt.setAccount(account);

    promptService.createPrompt(prompt);

    redirectAttributes.addFlashAttribute(
            "message",
            "Prompt created successfully");

    return "redirect:/prompts";
}


Method invocation 'getUserId' may produce 'NullPointerException' 

That's likely IntelliJ warning you that authentication.getPrincipal() is typed as Object, and after the cast it can't prove the result is non-null.

A safer version is:

Object principal = authentication.getPrincipal();

if (!(principal instanceof UserDetailsObject user)) {
    throw new IllegalStateException("Authenticated user not found");
}

PromptVaultUser account =
        promptVaultUserService.findUser(user.getUserId())
                .orElseThrow(() -> new IllegalArgumentException("User not found"));

Or even better, use @AuthenticationPrincipal, which avoids the cast entirely:

@PostMapping("/create")
public String createPrompt(
        @ModelAttribute("prompt") PromptCreateDto promptDto,
        @AuthenticationPrincipal UserDetailsObject user,
        RedirectAttributes redirectAttributes) {

    if (user == null) {
        throw new IllegalStateException("Authenticated user not found");
    }

    PromptVaultUser account =
            promptVaultUserService.findUser(user.getUserId())
                    .orElseThrow(() -> new IllegalArgumentException("User not found"));

    // ...
}

Import:

import org.springframework.security.core.annotation.AuthenticationPrincipal;

Since your entire application requires authentication except /req/** and static resources, a logged-in user should always exist according to your security configuration. The warning is more about static analysis than a real runtime issue. Using @AuthenticationPrincipal UserDetailsObject user is the cleanest approach.

InputSanitizer.java
File
Oh the @AuthenticationPrincipal fixed it. We should also make use of an input sanitiser to ensure that the user doesn't try anything suspicious with the title/text

Yes — you already have a good InputSanitizer for this. It uses Jsoup.clean(input, Safelist.none()).trim(), so it strips HTML/script content from plain text fields.

Inject it into PromptController:

private final InputSanitizer inputSanitizer;

Constructor:

public PromptController(
        PromptService promptService,
        PromptCategoryService promptCategoryService,
        PromptVaultUserService promptVaultUserService,
        InputSanitizer inputSanitizer) {
    this.promptService = promptService;
    this.promptCategoryService = promptCategoryService;
    this.promptVaultUserService = promptVaultUserService;
    this.inputSanitizer = inputSanitizer;
}

Import:

import me.winterbelle.prompvault.utils.helpers.security.InputSanitizer;

Then sanitize before saving:

Prompt prompt = new Prompt();
prompt.setTitle(inputSanitizer.sanitizePlainText(promptDto.getTitle()));
prompt.setPromptText(inputSanitizer.sanitizePlainText(promptDto.getPromptText()));
prompt.setCategory(category);
prompt.setVisibility(promptDto.getVisibility());
prompt.setAccount(account);

promptService.createPrompt(prompt);

So your create method should now use the sanitizer on:

promptDto.getTitle()
promptDto.getPromptText()

before setting them on the entity.

Users should be able to edit their own prompts. 
We need to make this prompt list better with cards. It should have a send button as you can see that we'll use later, a delete, and an edit button. We need to ensure a user can't try to edit or delete someone else's prompts 

I’ll keep the ownership check server-side, not just hidden in Thymeleaf. The key is: every edit/delete POST should load the prompt, compare its owner id to the authenticated user id, and redirect/refuse if it doesn’t match.

Yes. Your current card only has a send button , so add edit/delete buttons there, then enforce ownership in the controller/service.
prompt-card.html

<!DOCTYPE html>
<html xmlns:th="http://www.thymeleaf.org">
<body>

<div th:fragment="promptCard(prompt)"
     class="prompt-card">

    <div class="prompt-card-header">
        <h3 th:text="${prompt.title}">Title</h3>

        <span class="prompt-visibility"
              th:text="${prompt.visibility}">
            PRIVATE
        </span>
    </div>

    <p class="prompt-category"
       th:text="${prompt.category != null ? prompt.category.name : 'No Category'}">
        Category
    </p>

    <p class="prompt-text"
       th:text="${prompt.promptText}">

Add to PromptController

@GetMapping("/edit/{id}")
public String showEditPromptForm(
        @PathVariable Long id,
        @AuthenticationPrincipal UserDetailsObject user,
        Model model,
        RedirectAttributes redirectAttributes) {

    Prompt prompt = promptService.getPrompt(id);

    if (!prompt.getAccount().getId().equals(user.getUserId())) {
        redirectAttributes.addFlashAttribute(
                "message",
                "You cannot edit another user's prompt");

        return "redirect:/prompts";
    }

    PromptCreateDto promptDto = new PromptCreateDto();
    promptDto.setTitle(prompt.getTitle());
    promptDto.setPromptText(prompt.getPromptText());
    promptDto.setCategoryId(prompt.getCategory().getId());
    promptDto.setVisibility(prompt.getVisibility());

    model.addAttribute("prompt", promptDto);
    model.addAttribute("promptId", id);
    model.addAttribute("categories", promptCategoryService.getAllCategories());
    model.addAttribute("visibilities", Visibility.values());

    return "prompts/edit";
}

@PostMapping("/edit/{id}")
public String updatePrompt(
        @PathVariable Long id,
        @ModelAttribute("prompt") PromptCreateDto promptDto,
        @AuthenticationPrincipal UserDetailsObject user,
        RedirectAttributes redirectAttributes) {

    Prompt prompt = promptService.getPrompt(id);

    if (!prompt.getAccount().getId().equals(user.getUserId())) {
        redirectAttributes.addFlashAttribute(
                "message",
                "You cannot edit another user's prompt");

        return "redirect:/prompts";
    }

    PromptCategory category =
            promptCategoryService.getCategory(promptDto.getCategoryId());

    prompt.setTitle(inputSanitizer.sanitizePlainText(promptDto.getTitle()));
    prompt.setPromptText(inputSanitizer.sanitizePlainText(promptDto.getPromptText()));
    prompt.setCategory(category);
    prompt.setVisibility(promptDto.getVisibility());

    promptService.updatePrompt(prompt);

    redirectAttributes.addFlashAttribute(
            "message",
            "Prompt updated successfully");

    return "redirect:/prompts";
}

@PostMapping("/delete/{id}")
public String deletePrompt(
        @PathVariable Long id,
        @AuthenticationPrincipal UserDetailsObject user,
        RedirectAttributes redirectAttributes) {

    Prompt prompt = promptService.getPrompt(id);

    if (!prompt.getAccount().getId().equals(user.getUserId())) {
        redirectAttributes.addFlashAttribute(
                "message",
                "You cannot delete another user's prompt");

        return "redirect:/prompts";
    }

    promptService.deletePrompt(id);

    redirectAttributes.addFlashAttribute(
            "message",
            "Prompt deleted successfully");

    return "redirect:/prompts";
}

The important security part is not the buttons. It is these checks:

if (!prompt.getAccount().getId().equals(user.getUserId())) {
    return "redirect:/prompts";
}

That prevents someone manually typing /prompts/edit/7 or posting to /prompts/delete/7 for a prompt they do not own.

can't i re-use the create.html?

Absolutely. For a Spring Boot + Thymeleaf app like yours, I'd actually recommend reusing the same form.

A common pattern is:

    GET /prompts/create → empty DTO

    POST /prompts/create → create

    GET /prompts/edit/{id} → populated DTO

    POST /prompts/edit/{id} → update

Both GET methods return the same template:

return "prompts/form";

or even keep the name create.html if you want.
Controller

Create:

@GetMapping("/create")
public String showCreateForm(Model model) {

    model.addAttribute("prompt", new PromptCreateDto());
    model.addAttribute("categories", promptCategoryService.getAllCategories());
    model.addAttribute("visibilities", Visibility.values());

    model.addAttribute("isEdit", false);

    return "prompts/create";
}

Edit:

@GetMapping("/edit/{id}")
public String showEditForm(
        @PathVariable Long id,
        @AuthenticationPrincipal UserDetailsObject user,
        Model model) {

    Prompt prompt = promptService.getPrompt(id);

    if (!prompt.getAccount().getId().equals(user.getUserId())) {
        return "redirect:/prompts";
    }

    PromptCreateDto dto = new PromptCreateDto();
    dto.setTitle(prompt.getTitle());
    dto.setPromptText(prompt.getPromptText());
    dto.setCategoryId(prompt.getCategory().getId());
    dto.setVisibility(prompt.getVisibility());

    model.addAttribute("prompt", dto);
    model.addAttribute("categories", promptCategoryService.getAllCategories());
    model.addAttribute("visibilities", Visibility.values());

    model.addAttribute("isEdit", true);
    model.addAttribute("promptId", id);

    return "prompts/create";
}

Form action

In the HTML:

<form th:action="${isEdit}
                    ? '/prompts/edit/' + ${promptId}
                    : '/prompts/create'"
      th:object="${prompt}"
      method="post">

Or even cleaner:

Controller:

model.addAttribute(
        "formAction",
        "/prompts/create");

and

model.addAttribute(
        "formAction",
        "/prompts/edit/" + id);

Then HTML:

<form th:action="${formAction}"
      th:object="${prompt}"
      method="post">

Dynamic title/button

<h1 th:text="${isEdit ? 'Edit Prompt' : 'Create Prompt'}">
    Create Prompt
</h1>

<button type="submit"
        class="primary-btn"
        th:text="${isEdit ? 'Save Changes' : 'Create Prompt'}">
    Create Prompt
</button>

This avoids maintaining two nearly identical templates, which is usually the better design for CRUD forms. The only thing that changes between create and edit is:

    the DTO contents

    the form action URL

    the page/button text

Everything else is identical.

Fair point.

For your project, reuse create.html. Do not create an edit.html.
1. Add these model attributes in GET /create

model.addAttribute("prompt", new PromptCreateDto());
model.addAttribute("categories", promptCategoryService.getAllCategories());
model.addAttribute("visibilities", Visibility.values());

model.addAttribute("formAction", "/prompts/create");
model.addAttribute("pageTitle", "Create Prompt");
model.addAttribute("buttonText", "Create Prompt");

return "prompts/create";

2. Change your GET /edit/{id}

@GetMapping("/edit/{id}")
public String showEditPrompt(
        @PathVariable Long id,
        @AuthenticationPrincipal UserDetailsObject user,
        Model model) {

    Prompt prompt = promptService.getPrompt(id);

    if (!prompt.getAccount().getId().equals(user.getUserId())) {
        return "redirect:/prompts";
    }

    PromptCreateDto dto = new PromptCreateDto();
    dto.setTitle(prompt.getTitle());
    dto.setPromptText(prompt.getPromptText());
    dto.setCategoryId(prompt.getCategory().getId());
    dto.setVisibility(prompt.getVisibility());

    model.addAttribute("prompt", dto);
    model.addAttribute("categories", promptCategoryService.getAllCategories());
    model.addAttribute("visibilities", Visibility.values());

    model.addAttribute("formAction", "/prompts/edit/" + id);
    model.addAttribute("pageTitle", "Edit Prompt");
    model.addAttribute("buttonText", "Save Changes");

    return "prompts/create";
}

3. Add this update endpoint

@PostMapping("/edit/{id}")
public String updatePrompt(
        @PathVariable Long id,
        @ModelAttribute("prompt") PromptCreateDto dto,
        @AuthenticationPrincipal UserDetailsObject user,
        RedirectAttributes redirectAttributes) {

    Prompt prompt = promptService.getPrompt(id);

    if (!prompt.getAccount().getId().equals(user.getUserId())) {
        return "redirect:/prompts";
    }

    PromptCategory category =
            promptCategoryService.getCategory(dto.getCategoryId());

    prompt.setTitle(
            inputSanitizer.sanitizePlainText(dto.getTitle()));

    prompt.setPromptText(
            inputSanitizer.sanitizePlainText(dto.getPromptText()));

    prompt.setCategory(category);
    prompt.setVisibility(dto.getVisibility());

    promptService.updatePrompt(prompt);

    redirectAttributes.addFlashAttribute(
            "message",
            "Prompt updated successfully");

    return "redirect:/prompts";
}

4. Add this delete endpoint

@PostMapping("/delete/{id}")
public String deletePrompt(
        @PathVariable Long id,
        @AuthenticationPrincipal UserDetailsObject user,
        RedirectAttributes redirectAttributes) {

    Prompt prompt = promptService.getPrompt(id);

    if (!prompt.getAccount().getId().equals(user.getUserId())) {
        return "redirect:/prompts";
    }

    promptService.deletePrompt(id);

    redirectAttributes.addFlashAttribute(
            "message",
            "Prompt deleted successfully");

    return "redirect:/prompts";
}

5. Change your create.html

Replace the form tag:

<form th:action="@{${formAction}}"
      th:object="${prompt}"
      method="post">

Replace the title:

<h1 th:text="${pageTitle}">
    Create Prompt
</h1>

Replace the submit button:

<button type="submit"
        class="primary-btn"
        th:text="${buttonText}">
    Create Prompt
</button>

6. Add Edit/Delete buttons to prompt-card.html

<div class="prompt-actions">

    <form th:action="@{/prompts/send/{id}(id=${prompt.id})}"
          method="post">
        <button type="submit"
                class="primary-btn">
            Send
        </button>
    </form>

    <a th:href="@{/prompts/edit/{id}(id=${prompt.id})}"
       class="secondary-btn">
        Edit
    </a>

    <form th:action="@{/prompts/delete/{id}(id=${prompt.id})}"
          method="post">
        <button type="submit"
                class="danger-btn">
            Delete
        </button>
    </form>

</div>

That's the final implementation I'd use for PromptVault. One form page, ownership checks on edit/delete, and no duplicated templates.

PolicyKeyword(3).java

PolicyKeywordServiceImpl.java

FlaggedPrompt(3).java
