FlaggedPromptServiceImpl.java
File
We should scan prompts as they're being created to check if the title/text contains any keywords and create a flagged prompt for each matching keyword.
On edit we need to rescan and remove any that have been removed.
The card needs to show the user theflagged words they're containing as well

Given your existing model, I'd centralize this in FlaggedPromptService.

You already have:

    PolicyKeyword containing the keyword text

    FlaggedPrompt linking a Prompt to a collection of matching keywords

So add two methods:

void rescanPrompt(Prompt prompt);

String getKeywordTextForPrompt(Long promptId);

to FlaggedPromptService.
FlaggedPromptService

public interface FlaggedPromptService {

    List<FlaggedPromptDto> findAll();

    void rescanPrompt(Prompt prompt);

    String getKeywordTextForPrompt(Long promptId);
}

FlaggedPromptServiceImpl

Inject:

private final PolicyKeywordRepository policyKeywordRepository;
private final FlaggedPromptRepository flaggedPromptRepository;

Add:

@Override
@Transactional
public void rescanPrompt(Prompt prompt) {

    String content =
            (prompt.getTitle() + " " + prompt.getPromptText())
                    .toLowerCase();

    List<PolicyKeyword> matchedKeywords =
            policyKeywordRepository.findAll()
                    .stream()
                    .filter(keyword ->
                            content.contains(
                                    keyword.getText().toLowerCase()))
                    .toList();

    FlaggedPrompt existing =
            flaggedPromptRepository.findByPrompt(prompt)
                    .orElse(null);

    if (matchedKeywords.isEmpty()) {

        if (existing != null) {
            flaggedPromptRepository.delete(existing);
        }

        return;
    }

    if (existing == null) {
        existing = new FlaggedPrompt();
        existing.setPrompt(prompt);
    }

    existing.setKeywords(matchedKeywords);

    flaggedPromptRepository.save(existing);
}

Add:

@Override
public String getKeywordTextForPrompt(Long promptId) {

    return flaggedPromptRepository.findByPromptId(promptId)
            .map(flaggedPrompt ->
                    flaggedPrompt.getKeywords()
                            .stream()
                            .map(PolicyKeyword::getText)
                            .sorted()
                            .collect(Collectors.joining(", ")))
            .orElse("");
}

Repository additions

You'll need:

Optional<FlaggedPrompt> findByPrompt(Prompt prompt);

Optional<FlaggedPrompt> findByPromptId(Long promptId);

Create Prompt

Immediately after:

prompt = promptService.createPrompt(prompt);

call:

flaggedPromptService.rescanPrompt(prompt);

Edit Prompt

Immediately after:

promptService.updatePrompt(prompt);

call:

flaggedPromptService.rescanPrompt(prompt);

This automatically:

    creates a FlaggedPrompt if keywords are found

    updates the keyword list if changed

    removes the FlaggedPrompt entirely if all flagged words were removed

Prompt List

Instead of doing a lookup per card, add a field to your prompt DTO:

private String flaggedKeywords;

When building the list:

dto.setFlaggedKeywords(
        flaggedPromptService.getKeywordTextForPrompt(
                prompt.getId()));

prompt-card.html

Add directly below the category:

<div class="prompt-flags"
     th:if="${prompt.flaggedKeywords != null and !prompt.flaggedKeywords.isBlank()}">

    <strong>Flagged:</strong>

    <span th:text="${prompt.flaggedKeywords}">
        keyword1, keyword2
    </span>

</div>

CSS

.prompt-flags {
    margin-bottom: 15px;

    padding: 8px 12px;

    background: #fef3c7;

    border: 1px solid #f59e0b;
    border-radius: 8px;

    color: #92400e;

    font-size: .9rem;
}

This gives you:

    automatic scanning on create

    automatic rescanning on edit

    automatic cleanup when keywords disappear

    visible flagged keywords on the user's prompt cards

    no duplicated keyword logic in controllers.

    @GetMapping
    public String listPrompts(
            @AuthenticationPrincipal UserDetailsObject user,
            Model model) {

        model.addAttribute(
                "prompts",
                promptService.getPromptsForUser(user.getUserId()));

        return "prompts/list";
    }
I think I need something to work with that dto/flagged keywords

Yes. Right now your controller returns:

promptService.getPromptsForUser(user.getUserId())

which is returning List<Prompt>.

As soon as you want to display extra UI information that doesn't belong on the entity itself (flagged keywords, history count, last sent date, etc.), it's better to switch the list page to a DTO.

I'd create:

public record PromptListItemDto(
        Long id,
        String title,

attempting to delete a prompt gives an invocation target exception

InvocationTargetException is usually just a wrapper. The real error is buried further down the stack trace under:

Caused by: ...

For prompt deletion in your project, there are a few likely causes:
1. Prompt History references the Prompt

If PromptHistoryItem has:

@ManyToOne
@JoinColumn(name = "fk_prompt_id")
private Prompt prompt;

then deleting the prompt will violate a foreign key constraint if history records still exist.

You previously mentioned wanting to keep prompt history, so this is actually the most likely cause.

Typical underlying exception:

Caused by: org.hibernate.exception.ConstraintViolationException

or

Cannot delete or update a parent row:
a foreign key constraint fails

2. FlaggedPrompt references the Prompt

Your FlaggedPrompt has:

@OneToOne
@JoinColumn(name = "fk_prompt_id")
private Prompt prompt;

If a flagged record exists, the prompt cannot be deleted until the FlaggedPrompt is removed.

You'd need something like:

flaggedPromptRepository.findByPrompt(prompt)
        .ifPresent(flaggedPromptRepository::delete);

before deleting the prompt.
3. Ownership check passes, delete method is deleting null

Less likely, but possible if:

promptService.deletePrompt(id);

loads the prompt internally and gets null.
What I need to see

Show me:

PromptServiceImpl.deletePrompt(...)

and the full exception, especially everything after:

Caused by:

The InvocationTargetException itself is not the actual problem. The real exception is almost certainly a foreign key constraint involving either:

    PromptHistoryItem

    FlaggedPrompt

and once I see the delete method I can tell you exactly what needs changing.

Oh it's because it's a got some flagged prompts. We need to cascade deletes through there. 
    @Override
    public void deletePrompt(Long promptId) {
        promptRepository.deleteById(promptId);
    }

Yep. Since FlaggedPrompt has a foreign key to Prompt:

@OneToOne
@JoinColumn(name = "fk_prompt_id")
private Prompt prompt;

the database won't let you delete the prompt while the flagged prompt row still exists.

I would not use JPA cascade here because your FlaggedPrompt is more of a derived/moderation record than part of the prompt lifecycle. Instead, explicitly delete it first.

Add to FlaggedPromptRepository:

Optional<FlaggedPrompt> findByPrompt(Prompt prompt);

Then update PromptServiceImpl:

private final FlaggedPromptRepository flaggedPromptRepository;

Constructor:

public PromptServiceImpl(
        PromptRepository promptRepository,
        FlaggedPromptRepository flaggedPromptRepository) {

    this.promptRepository = promptRepository;
    this.flaggedPromptRepository = flaggedPromptRepository;
}

Delete method:

@Override
@Transactional
public void deletePrompt(Long promptId) {

    Prompt prompt = promptRepository.findById(promptId)
            .orElseThrow(() -> new IllegalArgumentException("Prompt not found"));

    flaggedPromptRepository.findByPrompt(prompt)
            .ifPresent(flaggedPromptRepository::delete);

    promptRepository.delete(prompt);
}

However, before you implement that, check whether you also have:

PromptHistoryItem -> Prompt

because earlier you mentioned wanting to keep prompt history.

If PromptHistoryItem has a foreign key to Prompt, then after fixing the flagged prompt issue you'll immediately hit another constraint violation from history records.

In that case I'd actually recommend soft deleting prompts later rather than physically deleting them, but for now show me PromptHistoryItem if prompt deletion still fails after removing the flagged prompt.

There can be multiple flagged prompts for a single prompt if it has multiple keywords

Looking at your model, that's actually not true with the current schema.

Your FlaggedPrompt is:

@OneToOne
@JoinColumn(name = "fk_prompt_id")
private Prompt prompt;

@ManyToMany
private List<PolicyKeyword> keywords;

That means:

    One Prompt

    One FlaggedPrompt

    Many PolicyKeywords attached to that flagged prompt

So a prompt containing:

hack
exploit
malware

should produce:

FlaggedPrompt #1
  Prompt -> My Prompt
  Keywords -> [hack, exploit, malware]

not:

FlaggedPrompt #1 -> hack
FlaggedPrompt #2 -> exploit
FlaggedPrompt #3 -> malware

In fact your admin DTO code already assumes this:

flaggedPrompt.getKeywords()
        .stream()
        .map(PolicyKeyword::getText)
        .collect(...)

and your keyword delete logic also assumes a single FlaggedPrompt contains multiple keywords:

flaggedPrompt.getKeywords().remove(keyword);

So for deletion you should only ever need:

Optional<FlaggedPrompt> findByPrompt(Prompt prompt);

and then:

flaggedPromptRepository.findByPrompt(prompt)
        .ifPresent(flaggedPromptRepository::delete);

If you're seeing multiple rows in flagged_prompts for the same prompt, then your rescanPrompt() implementation is creating duplicate FlaggedPrompt records instead of updating the existing one. In that case I'd want to see the current rescanPrompt() code because that's a bug in the scanning logic rather than the delete logic.

A quick check:

SELECT *
FROM flagged_prompts
WHERE fk_prompt_id = ?;

If that returns multiple rows for the same prompt, your database contents don't match the intended @OneToOne design.

Then add to FlaggedPromptService:

void rescanPrompt(Prompt prompt);

Implementation:

@Override
@Transactional
public void deleteByPrompt(Prompt prompt) {

    flaggedPromptRepository.findByPrompt(prompt)
            .ifPresent(flaggedPromptRepository::delete);
}

Now all flagged-prompt logic stays in one place:

    scanning

    keyword lookup

    deletion

and PromptServiceImpl only knows:

flaggedPromptService.getKeywordTextForPrompt(...)
flaggedPromptService.rescanPrompt(...)

which is much cleaner.

There's an even cleaner version, though.

The method:

String getKeywordTextForPrompt(Long promptId)

is really a UI concern, not a flagged prompt domain concern.

I'd actually move the DTO mapping:

Prompt -> PromptListItemDto

out of PromptServiceImpl entirely and into a dedicated mapper/service such as:

PromptListService

or

PromptDtoService

Then:

PromptService

handles prompt CRUD only.

FlaggedPromptService

handles moderation only.

PromptListService

builds UI DTOs.

For PromptVault at its current size, I'd stop at the first refactor and keep:

PromptServiceImpl
    -> PromptRepository
    -> FlaggedPromptService

but definitely remove the direct repository dependency.

Instead, pass where the request came from.
In My Prompts card

<form th:action="@{/prompts/send/{id}(id=${prompt.id})}"
      method="post">

    <input type="hidden"
           name="returnTo"
           value="mine"/>

    <button type="submit"
            class="primary-btn">
        Send
    </button>

</form>

In Shared Prompts card

<form th:action="@{/prompts/send/{id}(id=${prompt.id})}"
      method="post">

    <input type="hidden"
           name="returnTo"
           value="shared"/>

    <button type="submit"
            class="primary-btn">
        Send
    </button>

</form>

Controller

@PostMapping("/send/{id}")
public String sendPrompt(
        @PathVariable Long id,
        @RequestParam(defaultValue = "mine") String returnTo,
        RedirectAttributes redirectAttributes) {

    PromptHistoryItem result =
            promptService.sendPrompt(id);

    redirectAttributes.addFlashAttribute(
            "message",
            result.getResponseText());

    if ("shared".equals(returnTo)) {
        return "redirect:/prompts/shared";
    }

    return "redirect:/prompts";
}

This keeps the user on the page they were actually viewing, which is usually what feels most natural. It also continues to work if later you add things like:

    /prompts/category/{id}

    /prompts/search

    /prompts/history

because you can simply pass a different return value.

           name="returnTo"

@PostMapping("/send/{id}")
public String sendPrompt(

That way the exact same prompt-card.html works on both pages and automatically redirects back to the page it came from.

The issue is probably this Thymeleaf expression:

Thymeleaf sometimes behaves better with true comparisons. Change it to this:

<input type="hidden"
       name="returnTo"
       th:value="${isSharedView == true ? 'shared' : 'mine'}"/>

Also make sure your shared controller method definitely has:

model.addAttribute("isSharedView", true);

and your own prompts method has:

model.addAttribute("isSharedView", false);

<div th:replace="~{fragments/prompt-card :: promptCard(${prompt}, ${isSharedView})}">
</div>

     class="prompt-card">

            </button>

    The prompt text that was sent

    The AI response text

    createdAt / updatedAt inherited from AuditableEntity (based on your earlier refactor)

You already have a sidebar link for View Prompt History at /prompts/history , so I'd implement it very similarly to your existing prompt list page.
DTO

package me.winterbelle.prompvault.models.dto;

import java.time.LocalDateTime;

public class PromptHistoryItemDto {

    private Long id;
    private String promptText;
    private String responseText;
    private LocalDateTime createdAt;

    public Long getId() {
        return id;
    }

    public void setId(Long id) {
        this.id = id;
    }

    public String getPromptText() {
        return promptText;
    }

    public void setPromptText(String promptText) {
        this.promptText = promptText;
    }

    public String getResponseText() {
        return responseText;
    }

    public void setResponseText(String responseText) {
        this.responseText = responseText;
    }

    public LocalDateTime getCreatedAt() {
        return createdAt;
    }

    public void setCreatedAt(LocalDateTime createdAt) {
        this.createdAt = createdAt;
    }
}

Repository

package me.winterbelle.prompvault.repositories;

import me.winterbelle.prompvault.models.data.PromptHistoryItem;
import me.winterbelle.prompvault.models.data.PromptVaultUser;
import org.springframework.data.jpa.repository.JpaRepository;

import java.util.List;

public interface PromptHistoryItemRepository
        extends JpaRepository<PromptHistoryItem, Long> {

    List<PromptHistoryItem> findByAccountOrderByCreatedAtDesc(
            PromptVaultUser account
    );
}

Service

package me.winterbelle.prompvault.services;

import me.winterbelle.prompvault.models.dto.PromptHistoryItemDto;

import java.util.List;

public interface PromptHistoryService {

    List<PromptHistoryItemDto> getHistoryForCurrentUser();

}

ServiceImpl

package me.winterbelle.prompvault.services.impl;

import me.winterbelle.prompvault.models.data.PromptHistoryItem;
import me.winterbelle.prompvault.models.data.PromptVaultUser;
import me.winterbelle.prompvault.models.dto.PromptHistoryItemDto;
import me.winterbelle.prompvault.repositories.PromptHistoryItemRepository;
import me.winterbelle.prompvault.services.CurrentUserService;
import me.winterbelle.prompvault.services.PromptHistoryService;
import org.springframework.stereotype.Service;

import java.util.List;

@Service
public class PromptHistoryServiceImpl
        implements PromptHistoryService {

    private final PromptHistoryItemRepository repository;
    private final CurrentUserService currentUserService;

    public PromptHistoryServiceImpl(
            PromptHistoryItemRepository repository,
            CurrentUserService currentUserService
    ) {
        this.repository = repository;
        this.currentUserService = currentUserService;
    }

    @Override
    public List<PromptHistoryItemDto> getHistoryForCurrentUser() {

        PromptVaultUser user =
                currentUserService.getCurrentUser();

        return repository
                .findByAccountOrderByCreatedAtDesc(user)
                .stream()
                .map(this::toDto)
                .toList();
    }

    private PromptHistoryItemDto toDto(
            PromptHistoryItem item
    ) {

        PromptHistoryItemDto dto =
                new PromptHistoryItemDto();

        dto.setId(item.getId());
        dto.setPromptText(item.getPromptText());
        dto.setResponseText(item.getResponseText());
        dto.setCreatedAt(item.getCreatedAt());

        return dto;
    }
}

Controller

package me.winterbelle.prompvault.controllers;

import me.winterbelle.prompvault.services.PromptHistoryService;
import org.springframework.stereotype.Controller;
import org.springframework.ui.Model;
import org.springframework.web.bind.annotation.GetMapping;

@Controller
public class PromptHistoryController {

    private final PromptHistoryService historyService;

    public PromptHistoryController(
            PromptHistoryService historyService
    ) {
        this.historyService = historyService;
    }

    @GetMapping("/prompts/history")
    public String history(Model model) {

        model.addAttribute(
                "historyItems",
                historyService.getHistoryForCurrentUser()
        );

        return "prompts/history";
    }
}

I have a promptuserservice  that's better than the CurrentUserService you used there

Yes, after seeing your implementation I'd use your existing security setup instead.

Your UserDetailsObject already exposes the logged-in user's database ID via getUserId() and your PromptVaultUserService can retrieve a user by ID.

I'd update the service like this:

@Service
public class PromptHistoryServiceImpl
        implements PromptHistoryService {

    private final PromptHistoryItemRepository repository;
    private final PromptVaultUserService userService;

    public PromptHistoryServiceImpl(
            PromptHistoryItemRepository repository,
            PromptVaultUserService userService
    ) {
        this.repository = repository;
        this.userService = userService;
    }

    @Override
    public List<PromptHistoryItemDto> getHistoryForCurrentUser() {

        UserDetailsObject userDetails =
                (UserDetailsObject) SecurityContextHolder
                        .getContext()
                        .getAuthentication()
                        .getPrincipal();

        PromptVaultUser user =
                userService.findUser(userDetails.getUserId())
                        .orElseThrow();

        return repository
                .findByAccountOrderByCreatedAtDesc(user)
                .stream()
                .map(this::toDto)
                .toList();
    }

    private PromptHistoryItemDto toDto(
            PromptHistoryItem item
    ) {
        PromptHistoryItemDto dto =
                new PromptHistoryItemDto();

        dto.setId(item.getId());
        dto.setPromptText(item.getPromptText());
        dto.setResponseText(item.getResponseText());
        dto.setCreatedAt(item.getCreatedAt());

        return dto;
    }
}

Or even better, I'd avoid loading the entire user object at all and add a repository method:

List<PromptHistoryItem>
findByAccount_IdOrderByCreatedAtDesc(Long accountId);

Then:

UserDetailsObject userDetails =
        (UserDetailsObject) SecurityContextHolder
                .getContext()
                .getAuthentication()
                .getPrincipal();

return repository
        .findByAccount_IdOrderByCreatedAtDesc(
                userDetails.getUserId()
        )
        .stream()
        .map(this::toDto)
        .toList();

That's the approach I'd use in PromptVault because you're already storing the database user ID in the authenticated principal. It saves an extra database lookup and keeps the service simpler.

The service should be able to take a user Id and the controller should handle getting the current user, no?

Yes, that's generally the cleaner architecture.

The controller is responsible for web/security concerns (who is logged in).

The service is responsible for business logic (get history for a user).

I'd structure it like this:
Service

public interface PromptHistoryService {

    List<PromptHistoryItemDto> getHistoryForUser(Long userId);

}

ServiceImpl

@Override
public List<PromptHistoryItemDto> getHistoryForUser(Long userId) {

    return repository
            .findByAccount_IdOrderByCreatedAtDesc(userId)
            .stream()
            .map(this::toDto)
            .toList();
}

No SecurityContextHolder.
No UserDetailsObject.
No knowledge of authentication whatsoever.
Controller

@GetMapping("/prompts/history")
public String history(
        @AuthenticationPrincipal UserDetailsObject user,
        Model model
) {

    model.addAttribute(
            "historyItems",
            historyService.getHistoryForUser(
                    user.getUserId()
            )
    );

    return "prompts/history";
}

or if you prefer:

Authentication authentication =
        SecurityContextHolder.getContext()
                .getAuthentication();

UserDetailsObject user =
        (UserDetailsObject) authentication.getPrincipal();

inside the controller.

This gives you a few benefits:

    Service is reusable by admins later.

    Service can be unit tested without mocking Spring Security.

    Authentication concerns stay in the web layer.

    If you later add an admin view like:

/admin/users/{id}/history

you can simply do:

historyService.getHistoryForUser(id);

without changing the service.

For PromptVault, I'd definitely choose:

List<PromptHistoryItemDto> getHistoryForUser(Long userId)

rather than getHistoryForCurrentUser(). It keeps the service layer much cleaner.

Oh it looks like sending a prompt always takes the prompt's account but i could be sending a shared prompt. This should create the prompt history item for hte current user, not the prompt owner:
Service:    
@Override
    public PromptHistoryItem sendPrompt(Long promptId) {
        Prompt prompt = getPrompt(promptId);

        PromptHistoryItem historyItem = new PromptHistoryItem();

        historyItem.setAccount(prompt.getAccount());

        historyItem.setPromptText(prompt.getPromptText());

        historyItem.setResponseText(String.format("AI Service responded with 'TODO' at %s for prompt '%s'", LocalDateTime.now(), prompt.getPromptText()));

        return promptHistoryRepository.save(historyItem);
    }

Controller:
    @PostMapping("/send/{id}")
    public String sendPrompt(
            @PathVariable Long id,
            @RequestParam(defaultValue = "mine") String returnTo,
            RedirectAttributes redirectAttributes) {

        PromptHistoryItem result =
                promptService.sendPrompt(id);

        redirectAttributes.addFlashAttribute(
                "message",
                result.getResponseText());

        if ("shared".equals(returnTo)) {
            return "redirect:/prompts/shared";
        }

        return "redirect:/prompts";
    }

Yes — exactly. The Prompt owner should not automatically become the PromptHistoryItem owner.

Change sendPrompt so it takes the current user ID:

PromptHistoryItem sendPrompt(Long promptId, Long currentUserId);

ServiceImpl

@Override
public PromptHistoryItem sendPrompt(
        Long promptId,
        Long currentUserId
) {
    Prompt prompt = getPrompt(promptId);

    PromptVaultUser currentUser =
            promptVaultUserService.findUser(currentUserId)
                    .orElseThrow(() -> new IllegalArgumentException("User not found"));

    PromptHistoryItem historyItem = new PromptHistoryItem();

    historyItem.setAccount(currentUser);

    historyItem.setPromptText(prompt.getPromptText());

    historyItem.setResponseText(
            String.format(
                    "AI Service responded with 'TODO' at %s for prompt '%s'",
                    LocalDateTime.now(),
                    prompt.getPromptText()
            )
    );

    return promptHistoryRepository.save(historyItem);
}

Controller

@PostMapping("/send/{id}")
public String sendPrompt(
        @PathVariable Long id,
        @RequestParam(defaultValue = "mine") String returnTo,
        @AuthenticationPrincipal UserDetailsObject user,
        RedirectAttributes redirectAttributes
) {

    PromptHistoryItem result =
            promptService.sendPrompt(
                    id,
                    user.getUserId()
            );

    redirectAttributes.addFlashAttribute(
            "message",
            result.getResponseText()
    );

    if ("shared".equals(returnTo)) {
        return "redirect:/prompts/shared";
    }

    return "redirect:/prompts";
}

So the rule becomes:

historyItem.setAccount(currentUser);

not:

historyItem.setAccount(prompt.getAccount());

That way, if Beth sends one of Admin’s shared prompts, the history item belongs to Beth, not Admin.

For PromptVault, I'd lean toward making .main-content scrollable globally rather than making only the history page scrollable. It's simpler and tends to feel more consistent across pages like:

    My Prompts

All of those lists can eventually become long.

Prompt creation/update:
    @PostMapping("/create")
    public String createPrompt(
            @ModelAttribute("prompt") PromptDto promptDto,
            @AuthenticationPrincipal UserDetailsObject user,
            RedirectAttributes redirectAttributes) {

        PromptVaultUser account =
                promptVaultUserService.findUser(user.getUserId())
                        .orElseThrow(() -> new IllegalArgumentException("User not found"));

        PromptCategory category =
                promptCategoryService.findById(promptDto.getCategoryId());

        Prompt prompt = new Prompt();
        prompt.setTitle(inputSanitizer.sanitizePlainText(promptDto.getTitle()));
        prompt.setPromptText(inputSanitizer.sanitizePlainText(promptDto.getPromptText()));
        prompt.setCategory(category);
        prompt.setVisibility(promptDto.getVisibility());
        prompt.setAccount(account);

        prompt = promptService.createPrompt(prompt);
        flaggedPromptService.rescanPrompt(prompt);

        redirectAttributes.addFlashAttribute(
                "message",
                "Prompt created successfully");

        return "redirect:/prompts";
    }

@PostMapping("/edit/{id}")
    public String updatePrompt(
            @PathVariable Long id,
            @ModelAttribute("prompt") PromptDto dto,
            @AuthenticationPrincipal UserDetailsObject user,
            RedirectAttributes redirectAttributes) {

        Prompt prompt = promptService.getPrompt(id);

        if (!prompt.getAccount().getId().equals(user.getUserId())) {
            return "redirect:/prompts";
        }

        PromptCategory category =
                promptCategoryService.findById(dto.getCategoryId());

        prompt.setTitle(
                inputSanitizer.sanitizePlainText(dto.getTitle()));

        prompt.setPromptText(
                inputSanitizer.sanitizePlainText(dto.getPromptText()));

        prompt.setCategory(category);
        prompt.setVisibility(dto.getVisibility());

        prompt = promptService.updatePrompt(prompt);
        flaggedPromptService.rescanPrompt(prompt);

        redirectAttributes.addFlashAttribute(
                "message",
                "Prompt updated successfully");

        return "redirect:/prompts";
    }

We need to prevent a save when the title/text fields are empty

You should definitely validate this in three places:
1. DTO Validation (most important)

Add Bean Validation annotations to your PromptDto.

public class PromptDto {

    @NotBlank(message = "Title is required")
    private String title;

    @NotBlank(message = "Prompt text is required")
    private String promptText;

    @NotNull(message = "Category is required")
    private Long categoryId;

    @NotNull(message = "Visibility is required")
    private Visibility visibility;

    // getters/setters
}

2. Controller Validation

Use @Valid and BindingResult.
Create

@PostMapping("/create")
public String createPrompt(
        @Valid @ModelAttribute("prompt") PromptDto promptDto,
        BindingResult bindingResult,
        @AuthenticationPrincipal UserDetailsObject user,
        RedirectAttributes redirectAttributes,
        Model model) {

    if (bindingResult.hasErrors()) {

        model.addAttribute("categories",
                promptCategoryService.findAll());

        model.addAttribute("visibilities",
                Visibility.values());

        model.addAttribute("pageTitle",
                "Create Prompt");

        model.addAttribute("buttonText",
                "Create Prompt");

        model.addAttribute("formAction",
                "/prompts/create");

        return "prompts/create";
    }

    // existing save logic
}

Edit

Same idea:

@PostMapping("/edit/{id}")
public String updatePrompt(
        @PathVariable Long id,
        @Valid @ModelAttribute("prompt") PromptDto dto,
        BindingResult bindingResult,
        @AuthenticationPrincipal UserDetailsObject user,
        RedirectAttributes redirectAttributes,
        Model model) {

    if (bindingResult.hasErrors()) {

        model.addAttribute("categories",
                promptCategoryService.findAll());

        model.addAttribute("visibilities",
                Visibility.values());

        model.addAttribute("pageTitle",
                "Edit Prompt");

        model.addAttribute("buttonText",
                "Save Changes");

        model.addAttribute("formAction",
                "/prompts/edit/" + id);

        return "prompts/create";
    }

    // existing update logic
}

3. Handle Sanitization Edge Case

This is the one people usually miss.

A user can enter:

     

or

<script>alert('x')</script>

and after sanitization the result may become blank.

So after:

String title =
        inputSanitizer.sanitizePlainText(promptDto.getTitle());

String promptText =
        inputSanitizer.sanitizePlainText(promptDto.getPromptText());

check:

if (title.isBlank() || promptText.isBlank()) {

    bindingResult.reject(
            "prompt.invalid",
            "Title and prompt text cannot be empty"
    );

    // return form
}

Without this check, a malicious user can bypass the HTML required attribute and end up saving an empty prompt.
4. Display Validation Messages

Under the fields:

<input th:field="*{title}" />

<div class="validation-message error"
     th:if="${#fields.hasErrors('title')}"
     th:errors="*{title}">
</div>

and

<textarea th:field="*{promptText}"></textarea>

<div class="validation-message error"
     th:if="${#fields.hasErrors('promptText')}"
     th:errors="*{promptText}">
</div>

This gives you:

    Browser-side validation (required)

    DTO validation (@NotBlank)

    Server-side validation (@Valid)

    Protection against whitespace-only and sanitization-to-empty inputs

That's the combination I'd use for PromptVault.
